< Review>
I’m new to the area, saw 4.9 stars and was super excited to eat here. Almost no cooked food menu, $18.00 Mixed tempura... sure, why not? Oops, that wasn’t worth $8.00. Miso was typical, $3.00 bowl of rice that tasted like cardboard, but had a decent consistency. Sushi was typical, not great, but fine. $8.00 for a Japanese Scallop that was the best thing I tried, but not good enough to order again. The finishing touch was a salmon skin hand roll that wasn’t crispy and the salmon skin was cold. I assume this was cooked in advance and put in the countertop cooling system. The place was pretty busy and most appeared to be known to the waitress. Waitress was nice, sweet and works very efficiently. I spent $71.00 trying different things by myself and I have to say my wife was the lucky one because she stayed home.</Review>

<text>I happily wrote a five star review after Mark's email reminder requesting a review because we truly had a good shopping experience, but 9 months after purchasing our fitness equipments, but I have to downgrade for several reasons.
1. Low quality products  -  The installation team had to come twice because the first batch of Procor equipments (an Elliptical and a treadmill) were not functioning. The inclination on Elliptical stopped working after 6 months of installation, and inclination on treadmill stopped working after nine months with treadmill very lightly used. We got the inclination on treadmill back to work by turning the power off and back on, but then a new problem started - When nobody was using the machine and it should be idle, the treadmill would adjust the inclination on its own every 30 seconds or so for several minutes, go back to normal, then all of sudden start adjusting again...
2. Very unfriendly after-purchase conversation (not with Mark, with the other salesperson, Reece I believe) - When I called to complain about the quality of the equipments and request the contact info of the service people, Reece insisted that I shouldn't call the machine broken, "Inclination not working doesn't mean the machine is broken, it means the machine has issues, but not broken and Precor has very strong warranty that nobody else can match". We almost got into an argument and I had to stop him and ask for the contact info of the service people. I'm not sure if it was a bad day for him, but I certainly didn't expect that. BTW, the very strong warranty that nobody else can match is 10 years on parts and 1 year on labor, which is standard, and with the speed of the service (elaborated below), the 1 year labor really doesn't mean much.
3. Non-functional in-contract repair service - We contacted the service team for the inclination on Elliptical in June. They were very responsive in getting back to us, but very slow in scheduling visits, probably because they are very busy (I could be wrong, but my understanding is this 2-person team is the only one for this half of the bay area). The worst part is that they don't seem to be able to get the problem fixed. After three months and three visits, the inclination on our Elliptical is still not working. And on the inclination of the treadmill, they ran a diagnostic but couldn't detect any problem and assured us the machine is totally fine. But I know there's a problem because I watched and even shot a video of the treadmill adjusting inclination on it's own when it's supposed to be idle. But when the only service team available said there wasn't a problem, the only thing we could do is to shut down the machine after each use to prevent more damage that may eventually break the machine. I don't want to blame the service team because they seem to be very willing to help, but the net result is truly very disappointing.
One last thing I want to add to my review is that we did have very nice experience making the purchase, bought one Precor treadmill, one Precor Elliptical and one Inspire conditioning combo.
Our purchasing experience with Mark was still good. He was knowledgeable and wasn't pushy. That's why I'm giving a three star instead of one.

<Text>Hole in the wall awesome boba find!

Your choice of milk teas, slush, snowy milk, and smoothies plus coffee or regular tea. They all come in what my friends and I titled “Buckets ‘o’ Boba” - large, fat containers that you can supersize for $.95 extra. Your choice of dairy or almond milk. They have numerous jellies and puddings you can add, but the boba itself tastes fresh, is perfectly chewy and just the right amount. Did I mention they also have card & board games available?

<Review>Boba Cha Cha is probably one of the best places to get boba. The boba pearls are always fresh and they just taste great, unlike some other places around the area. The menu has several options for any type of taste.
The atmosphere is quite friendly, everyone working there is kind and helpful. This is also the perfect place to hang out with friends and family as the location provides costumers with a variety of boardgames.
The place usually gets busy in the afternoon, when all the high school students decide to stop for a drink.
The only pain is the limited parking space and the constant traffic around that area. But if you just happened to find a spot, you can treat yourself to a nice and cool drink.</Review>< pics>

This is coming from someone who used to not like Boba. The lady still remembers exactly how I like mine. I think with enough marketing and a few risks they can open multiple locations in the next few years.< /Review>
